        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct Superassemblies of Freestanding Metal-Carbon Frameworks Featuring Reversible Crystalline-Phase Transformation for Electrochemical Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Biao; Zu, Lianhai; Peng, Chengxin; Zhang, Yan; Zhang, Wei; Tang, Jing; Selomulya, Cordelia; Zhang, Liudi; Chen, Hanxing; Wang, Yang; Liu, Yang; He, Haili; Wei, Jing; Lin, Xiaocheng; Luo, Wei; Yang, Jianping; Zhao, Zaiwang; Liu, Yong; Yang, Jinhu; Zhao, Dongyuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">50</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16533-16541</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with long-term cycling attract increasing attention for large-scale energy storage.  However, traditional SIBs toward practical applications still suffer from low rate capability and poor cycle induced by pulverization and amorphorization of anodes at high rate (over 5 C) during the fast ion insertion/extn. process.  The present work demonstrates a robust strategy for a variety of (Sb-C, Bi-C, Sn-C, Ge-C, Sb-Bi-C) freestanding metal-carbon framework thin films via a space-confined superassembly (SCSA) strategy.  The sodium-ion battery employing the Sb-C framework exhibits an unprecedented performance with a high specific capacity of 246 mAh/g, long life cycle (5000 cycles), and superb capacity retention (almost 100%) at a high rate of 7.5 C (3.51A/g).  Further investigation indicates that the unique framework structure enables unusual reversible cryst.-phase transformation, guaranteeing the fast and long-cyclability sodium storage.  This study may open an avenue to developing long-cycle-life and high-power SIBs for practical energy applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqK5sMN8Rb52rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixuBsnh8Qosg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitVCjsb7P&amp;md5=37b51d2617e79080500d7a0178354f67</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.03.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Highly Stable (SnO<sub>x</sub>-Sn)@Few Layered Graphene Composite Anode of Sodium-Ion Batteries Synthesized by Oxygen Plasma Assisted Milling</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly stable (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene composite anode of sodium-ion batteries synthesized by oxygen plasma assisted milling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Deliang; Liu, Jiangwen; Li, Xiang; Hu, Renzong; Zeng, Meiqing; Yang, Lichun; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">350</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1-8</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene ((SnOx-Sn)@FLG) composite has been synthesized by O plasma-assisted milling.  Owing to the synergistic effect of rapid plasma heating and ball mill grinding, SnOx (1≤ x ≤2) nanoparticles generated from the reaction of Sn with O are tightly wrapped by FLG nanosheets which are simultaneously exfoliated from expanded graphite, forming secondary micro granules.  Inside the granules, the small size of the SnOx nanoparticles enables the fast kinetics for Na+ transfer.  The in-situ formed FLG and residual Sn nanoparticles improve the elec. cond. of the composite, meanwhile alleviate the aggregation of SnOx nanoparticles and relieve the vol. change during the cycling, which is beneficial for the cyclic stability for the Na+ storage.  As an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 448 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g in the 1st cycle, with 82.6% capacity retention after 250 cycles.  Even when the c.d. increases to 1000 mA/g, this composite retains 316.5 mAh/g after 250 cycles.  With superior Na+ storage stability, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite can be a promising anode material for high performance sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpu3VJ7Z_IUi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixuBsnh8Qosg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkslyjtrY%253D&amp;md5=411e9333c9fa824c27eb67deca3362e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b14233"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal–Organic Framework-Derived NiSb Alloy Embedded in Carbon Hollow Spheres as Superior Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New Nanoconfined Galvanic Replacement Synthesis of Hollow Sb@C Yolk-Shell Spheres Constituting a Stable Anode for High-Rate Li/Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jun; Yu, Litao; Wu, Chao; Wen, Yuren; Yin, Kuibo; Chiang, Fu-Kuo; Hu, Renzong; Liu, Jiangwen; Sun, Litao; Gu, Lin; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2034-2042</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the current research project, we have prepd. a novel Sb@C nanosphere anode with biomimetic yolk-shell structure for Li/Na-ion batteries via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement route.  The yolk-shell microstructure consists of Sb hollow yolk completely protected by a well-conductive carbon thin shell.  The substantial void space in the these hollow Sb@C yolk-shell particles allows for the full vol. expansion of inner Sb while maintaining the framework of the Sb@C anode and developing a stable SEI film on the outside carbon shell.  As for Li-ion battery anode, they displayed a large specific capacity (634 mAh/g), high rate capability (specific capabilities of 622, 557, 496, 439, and 384 mAh/g at 100, 200, 500, 1000, and 2000 mA/g, resp.) and stable cycling performance (a specific capacity of 405 mAh/g after long 300 cycles at 1000 mA/g).  As for Na-ion storage, these yolk-shell Sb@C particles also maintained a reversible capacity of approx. 280 mAh/g at 1000 mA/g after 200 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1-cHFJgjO0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhImVlNai9kVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXisVOrtbk%253D&amp;md5=e03ea2baddc606a4ea8f0a430060e439</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Darwiche, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Marino, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sougrati, M. T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fraisse, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stievano, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Monconduit, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Am. Chem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">134</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">20805</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">20811</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja310347x</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D134%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D20805-20811%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DA.%2BDarwiche%26author%3DC.%2BMarino%26author%3DM.%2BT.%2BSougrati%26author%3DB.%2BFraisse%26author%3DL.%2BStievano%26author%3DL.%2BMonconduit%26title%3DBetter%2BCycling%2BPerformances%2Bof%2BBulk%2BSb%2Bin%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%2BCompared%2Bto%2BLi-Ion%2BSystems%253A%2BAn%2BUnexpected%2BElectrochemical%2BMechanism%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fja310347x&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b07964&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fja310347x&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhImVlNai9kVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.03.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Si, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemical Bonding Between Antimony and Ionic Liquid-Derived Nitrogen-Doped Carbon for Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical bonding between antimony and ionic liquid-derived nitrogen-doped carbon for sodium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xin; Si, Ling; Zhou, Xiaosi; Tu, Fengzhang; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">349</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">37-44</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony has received a great deal of attention as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, this application is significantly hampered by inherent large vol. change and sluggish kinetics.  To address these issues, an antimony-cyano-based ionic liq.-derived nitrogen-doped carbon (Sb-CNC) hybrid is proposed and synthesized by ball-milling and subsequent pyrolysis treatment.  As an anode material for SIBs, the as-synthesized Sb-CNC hybrid delivers reversible capacities of 475 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and 203 mAh g-1 at 5000 mA g-1, and a 92.4% capacity retention based on the first-cycle capacity after 150 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  Using ex situ XPS and elemental mapping techniques, we attribute the good structural integrity to the formation of Sb-N-C bonds between Sb and the cyano-based ionic liq.-derived N-doped carbon matrix.  Moreover, the presence of N-doped carbon network in the hybrid material serves as a robust protective cover and an elec. highway, buffering the substantial vol. expansion of Sb nanoparticles and ensuring the fast electron transport for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0rTJNqWEUn7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhImVlNai9kVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktVKmsLc%253D&amp;md5=bdba7a23cb25ed9d8053b89fd94d27e2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA03434B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Si, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Uniformly-Distributed Sb Nanoparticles in Ionic Liquid-Derived Nitrogen-Enriched Carbon for Highly Reversible Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniformly-distributed Sb nanoparticles in ionic liquid-derived nitrogen-enriched carbon for highly reversible sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xin; Dou, Zhifeng; Gu, Erlong; Si, Ling; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13411-13420</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antinomy has received considerable attention as one of the most promising anode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity and suitable working voltage.  However, the large vol. change of Sb during the alloying/dealloying process causes poor cycling stability and low rate capability, which hinder its practical application.  Here, the authors substantially enhance the Na storage performance of Sb by binding Sb nanoparticles in ionic liq.-derived N-enriched C (Sb@NC) via pyrolysis of an SbCl3/1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium dicyanamide mixt.  The Sb@NC composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 440 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, superior rate performance of 285 and 237 mA h g-1 at the high current densities of 2 and 5 A g-1, resp., and greatly improved cycle life of 328 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 100 A g-1 after 300 cycles in the half cell of SIBs.  In the full cell, the energy d. of Sb@NC//Na3V2(PO4)3/C is ∼147 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 50 W kg-1.  Even at 2.37 kW kg-1, an energy d. of ∼65 W h kg-1 is still retained.  The remarkably improved electrochem. performance could be assigned to the synergistic effect of nanoscale size, uniform distribution, and chem. coupling effect between Sb and ionic liq.-derived N-enriched C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqodGGRdGl-4rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhImVlNai9kVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXosVCltrg%253D&amp;md5=58676af0e3ee4eb633c74aea69719a47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms3922"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, D.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity antimony sulphide nanoparticle-decorated graphene composite as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu Denis Y W; Prikhodchenko Petr V; Mason Chad W; Batabyal Sudip K; Gun Jenny; Sladkevich Sergey; Medvedev Alexander G; Lev Ovadia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).  The energy density could exceed that of some lithium-ion batteries with further optimization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGZMXlr7vNCe3MPKNEWB5RfW6udTcc2eac8PhjQObaFrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c3ltFajuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=00d6ac79468675541d9951b7cfb704e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b03920"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Chemically Coupled Antimony/Multilayer Graphene Hybrid as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Chemically Coupled Antimony/Multilayer Graphene Hybrid as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Lingyun; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Du, Yichen; Li, Yafei; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8138-8145</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted considerable attention as a promising alternative to Li-ion batteries owing to the natural abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for Na-ion batteries, Sb is a desirable candidate due to its high theor. capacity (660 mA h g-1).  Herein, an Sb/multilayer graphene hybrid, in which Sb is homogeneously anchored on multilayer graphene, is produced by a confined vapor deposition method.  The chem. bonding can realize robust and intimate contact between Sb and multilayer graphene, and the uniform distribution of Sb and the highly conductive and flexible multilayer graphene can not only improve Na ion diffusion and electronic transport but also stabilize the solid electrolyte interphase upon the large vol. changes of Sb during cycling.  Consequently, the Sb/multilayer graphene hybrid shows a high reversible Na storage capacity (452 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1), stable long-term cycling performance with 90% capacity retention after 200 cycles, and excellent rate capability (210 mA h g-1 under 5000 mA g-1).  This facile synthesis approach and unique nanostructure can potentially be extended to other alloy materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDfBd8kZiyFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCsEyBxRMA_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVCjtb7K&amp;md5=2d783871704dc4fcc47474721f1b1ab3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta13438e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dai, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.-G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Wet Milled Synthesis of an Sb/MWCNT Nanocomposite for Improved Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical properties and morphological evolution of pitaya-like Sb@C microspheres as high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Lin; Lu, Haiyan; Xiao, Lifen; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pitaya-like Sb@C microspheres are prepd. successfully by facile aerosol spray drying synthesis.  Structural and morphol. characterizations reveal that the Sb@C microspheres have a uniform pitaya-like structure, with well crystd. Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the C matrix.  The Sb@C microsphere electrodes exhibit high Na storage capacity of 655 mA h g-1 at C/15 with excellent cyclability (93% of capacity retention over 100 cycles), as well as good rate capability.  Also, the morphol. evolution of the Sb@C microspheres is studied to account for its excellent electrochem. performance, caused by maintenance of the pitaya-like configuration during cycling.  This structural stability guarantees tight contact of Sb with C buffer, as well as uniform distribution of Sb to balance the localized mech. stress, ensuring excellent electrochem. performance.  The structural design and synthetic method reported in this work may provide an effective way to stabilize electrochem. performance of Na-storable alloy materials and therefore provide a new prospect for creation of cycle-stable alloy anodes for high capacity Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo57lFV_VztT7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgCsEyBxRMA_g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb Nanoparticles Encapsulated in a Reticular Amorphous Carbon Network for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Min; Yang, Zhenzhong; Wang, Jiaqing; Li, Weihan; Gu, Lin; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb@3D RCN (Reticular Carbon Network) films were prepd. through electrostatic spray deposition.  The encapsulating nanosized Sb in reticular porous carbon network enables excellent storage properties with respect to Na.  More specifically, at 0.2 C the Sb@3D RCN film electrode delivers a reversible capacity of 630 mA h g-1, approaching 96% of its theor. capacity.  Cycle stability tests conducted at a rate of 3 C exhibit a reversible capacity of 224 mA h g-1 after 900 cycles.  This performance is attributed to the unique Sb@3D RCN: (i) the carbon matrix prevents Sb nanoparticles agglomeration upon prolonged cycling; (ii) the large void space within 3D RCN may buffer the vol. expansion, leading to the high cycling stability of the electrode material; and (iii) the reticular structure ensures fast transport of the electrolyte within the electrode.  This structure design can be further extended to build up various nanomaterials with this unique reticular core-shell structure for promising applications in catalysis, sensing, supercapacitors, and fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQ7O0ZLDjepLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lji88LdimwOcg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural Effect on Electrochemical Performance of Ordered Porous Carbon Electrodes for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jo, Changshin; Park, Yuwon; Jeong, Jooyoung; Lee, Kyu Tae; Lee, Jinwoo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ordered meso- or macro-porous carbons (OMCs) were applied as anodes in Na ion battery (NIB) systems.  Three different block copolymers (BCPs) enabled us to control the pore sizes (6, 33, and 60 nm) while maintaining the same 2-D hexagonal structure.  To exclude other effects, the factors including precursors, particle sizes, and degrees of graphitization were controlled.  The structures of OMCs were characterized by nitrogen physisorption, Raman spectroscopy, X-ray analyses (XRD and SAXS), and microscopies (TEM and SEM).                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Rich Mesoporous Carbon as Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Sun, Ning; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Zhu, Qizhen; Wu, Feng; Qiao, Ning; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-rich carbon with interconnected mesoporous structure has been simply prepd. via a nano-CaCO3 template method, using polyaniline as carbon and nitrogen precursors.  The prepn. process includes in situ polymn. of aniline in a nano-CaCO3 aq. soln., carbonization of the composites and removal of the template with dild. hydrochloric acid.  Nitrogen sorption shows the carbon-enriched mesopores with a sp. surface area of 113 m2 g-1.  The XPS anal. indicates that the carbon has a high nitrogen content of 7.78 at.%, in the forms of pyridinic and pyrrolic, as well as graphitic nitrogen.  The nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon shows a high reversible capacity of 338 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 30 mA g-1, and good rate performance as well as ultralong cycling durability (110.7 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 500 mA g-1 over 800 cycles).  The excellent sodium storage performance of the nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon is attributed to its disordered structure with large interlayer distance, interconnected porosity, and the enriched nitrogen heteroatoms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwkJbCuGMkELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFhGrhTWDbHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOrtr3M&amp;md5=26b08a49898c6e6ae937f4de90e676f6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/adma.200801492"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stein, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fierke, M.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Malachite green adsorption by potassium salts-activated carbons derived from textile sludge: Equilibrium, kinetics and thermodynamics studies</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This work is aimed at evaluating the adsorption of malachite green (MG) on potassium salts-activated carbons derived from textile sludge.  Potassium hydroxide (KOH), potassium iodide (KI), and the potassium salts (KOH + KI) composite were used in chem. activation.  The physicochem. properties of the activated carbons were characterized according to textural and surface chem.  The sp. surface area of activated carbon is in the range of 66 to 584 m2/g.  The KOH and KI + KOH composite series exhibit a higher surface area.  The max. MG adsorption are between 167 and 113 mg/g.  Langmuir model shows the best conformity to the equil. data, while the kinetics data were best fitted to the pseudo-second-order model, suggesting the chemisorption process.  The intraparticle diffusion maybe involved, but it is not the sole rate-limiting step, while the film diffusion could be the controlling mechanism.  Thermodn. data revealed that the MG adsorption is spontaneous and endothermic.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a KOH self-templating synthesis of three-dimensional hierarchical porous carbon using resol as the precursor and KOH as both the template and activating agent.  The resulting resol-derived porous carbon (RPC) exhibits a high surface area (up to 2700 m2/g) and well-interconnected macropores with micropores and mesopores decorated on the carbon walls.  Consequently, the RPC shows low internal resistance, high specific capacitance, good rate capability and excellent cycling stability in 6 M KOH as a supercapacitor electrode.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Carbon foams are reviewed by focusing on their prepn. and application.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Porous N-Doped Graphene Frameworks Made of Interconnected Nanocages for Ultrahigh-Rate and Long-Life Li-O2 Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Changtai; Yu, Chang; Liu, Shaohong; Yang, Juan; Fan, Xiaoming; Huang, Huawei; Qiu, Jieshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6913-6920</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The inferior rate capability and poor cycle stability of the present Li-O2 batteries are still crit. obstacles for practice applications.  Configuring novel and integrated air electrode materials with unique structure and tunable chem. compns. is one of the efficient strategies to solve these bottleneck problems.  Herein, a novel strategy for synthesis of 3-dimensional porous N-doped graphene aerogels (NPGAs) with frameworks constructed by interconnected nanocages with the aid of polystyrene sphere@polydopamine is reported.  The interconnected nanocages as the basic building unit of graphene sheets are assembled inside the skeletons of 3-dimensional graphene aerogels, leading to the 3-dimensional NPGA with well-developed interconnected channels and the full exposure of electrochem. active sites.  Benefiting from such an unique structure, the as-made NPGA delivers a high specific capacity, an excellent rate capacity of 5978 mA-h g-1 at 3.2 A g-1, and long cycle stability, esp. at a large c.d. (54 cycles at 1 A g-1), indicative of boosted rate capability and cycle life as air electrodes for Li-O2 batteries.  More importantly, based on the total mass of C+Li2O2, a gravimetric energy d. of 2400 W h kg-1 for the NPGA-O2//Li cell is delivered at a power d. of 1300 W kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_VKX1ezY-r7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liFSMNHZ46ICA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1yksrvL&amp;md5=9d298dc194a6716507ad8733878df3ec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b06898"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiao, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Rich Mesoporous Carbon as Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Rich Mesoporous Carbon as Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Sun, Ning; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Zhu, Qizhen; Wu, Feng; Qiao, Ning; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">49</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-rich carbon with interconnected mesoporous structure has been simply prepd. via a nano-CaCO3 template method, using polyaniline as carbon and nitrogen precursors.  The prepn. process includes in situ polymn. of aniline in a nano-CaCO3 aq. soln., carbonization of the composites and removal of the template with dild. hydrochloric acid.  Nitrogen sorption shows the carbon-enriched mesopores with a sp. surface area of 113 m2 g-1.  The XPS anal. indicates that the carbon has a high nitrogen content of 7.78 at.%, in the forms of pyridinic and pyrrolic, as well as graphitic nitrogen.  The nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon shows a high reversible capacity of 338 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 30 mA g-1, and good rate performance as well as ultralong cycling durability (110.7 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 500 mA g-1 over 800 cycles).  The excellent sodium storage performance of the nitrogen-rich mesoporous carbon is attributed to its disordered structure with large interlayer distance, interconnected porosity, and the enriched nitrogen heteroatoms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwkJbCuGMkELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liFSMNHZ46ICA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOrtr3M&amp;md5=26b08a49898c6e6ae937f4de90e676f6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1021/ja907098f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb-C nanofibers with long cycle life as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Lin; Hu, Xiaohong; Qian, Jiangfeng; Pei, Feng; Wu, Fayuan; Mao, Rongjun; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform nanofiber structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon nanofibers.  Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).  The superior electrochem. performances of the Sb-C nanofibers are due to the unique nanofiber structure and uniform distribution of Sb nanoparticles in carbon matrix, which provides a conductive and buffering matrix for effective release of mech. stress caused by Na ion insertion/extn. and prevent the aggregation of the Sb nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqODsgQsiGAJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSBriXsE-Q_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFKhtrrN&amp;md5=b043a6265ebe5b5183098fbd4c98cc1f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b03920"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Chemically Coupled Antimony/Multilayer Graphene Hybrid as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Chemically Coupled Antimony/Multilayer Graphene Hybrid as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Lingyun; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Du, Yichen; Li, Yafei; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8138-8145</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted considerable attention as a promising alternative to Li-ion batteries owing to the natural abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for Na-ion batteries, Sb is a desirable candidate due to its high theor. capacity (660 mA h g-1).  Herein, an Sb/multilayer graphene hybrid, in which Sb is homogeneously anchored on multilayer graphene, is produced by a confined vapor deposition method.  The chem. bonding can realize robust and intimate contact between Sb and multilayer graphene, and the uniform distribution of Sb and the highly conductive and flexible multilayer graphene can not only improve Na ion diffusion and electronic transport but also stabilize the solid electrolyte interphase upon the large vol. changes of Sb during cycling.  Consequently, the Sb/multilayer graphene hybrid shows a high reversible Na storage capacity (452 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1), stable long-term cycling performance with 90% capacity retention after 200 cycles, and excellent rate capability (210 mA h g-1 under 5000 mA g-1).  This facile synthesis approach and unique nanostructure can potentially be extended to other alloy materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDfBd8kZiyFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSBriXsE-Q_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVCjtb7K&amp;md5=2d783871704dc4fcc47474721f1b1ab3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC05275G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ko, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrafine Sb nanocrystals, uniformly distributed in a C matrix with a microspherical morphol., were synthesized by 1-pot spray pyrolysis.  The Sb-C composite microspheres exhibited good Na-storage properties with stable cyclability, a capacity retention of 90% over 100 cycles, and good rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVMzaktIdv1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSBriXsE-Q_Q"> &gt;&gt; Future outlook of sodium-ion batteries is discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_Iht8id70u7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lisZRVxBiNIbw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFSiu7bL&amp;md5=d4497339c61083b2ec2c0568261e4909</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2015.09.091"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Balogun, M.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tong, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Review of Carbon Materials and Their Composites with Alloy Metals for Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Carbon</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">98</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">162</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">178</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.carbon.2015.09.091</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of carbon materials and their composites with alloy metals for sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Balogun, Muhammad-Sadeeq; Luo, Yang; Qiu, Weitao; Liu, Peng; Tong, Yexiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">98</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">162-178</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are currently emerging as a replacement for lithium ion batteries due to sodium abundance in the earth's crust.  The recent development of sodium ion batteries anode has been achieved by the use of selected carbon as an anode.  The performance of the selected carbon materials such as the charge/discharge capacity, voltage profile and cyclic stability, depend strongly on the sizes, additives, electrolytes and structures.  Based on the contribution of the carbon-based materials as a replacement of the sodium ion batteries anode, much improvement has been achieved.  However, more investigations are still required in order to identify the suitable carbon materials that can provide and improve the anode properties.  In the same vein, alloy materials have gained increasing effort as high capacity anode and their combination with carbon have contributed to the development of sodium ion batteries.  In this review, we have accounted for the development of carbon-based materials and their composites with alloy materials as well as their prospects and challenges for sodium ion battery anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLqTy97T_9sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpaZ4TBerBCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVOmsbvM&amp;md5=5bc4c118e6be905d663496bf2953e8d7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700606"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chou, S.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.-X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advances and Challenges in Metal Sulfides/Selenides for Next-Generation Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1700606</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ceder, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges for Na-Ion Negative Electrodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Electrochem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">158</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">A1011</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">A1014</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/1.3607983</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Challenges for Na-ion Negative Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chevrier, V. L.; Ceder, G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">158</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A1011-A1014</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been proposed as candidates for replacing Li-ion batteries.  The authors examine the viability of Na-ion anode materials based on Na alloys or hard carbons in terms of volumetric energy d.  Due to the bigger size of the Na atom compared to the Li atom, Na alloys would lead to anode materials with about half the volumetric energy d. of their Li analogs.  Volumetric energy densities obtainable with sodiated hard carbons would also be significantly less than those obtainable with lithiated graphite.  These findings highlight the need of novel ideas for Na-ion anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfbyHmIC7uUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpaZ4TBerBCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXpt1Ont7c%253D&amp;md5=f132981922c6ce146def4cd54c721e2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201600846"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">You, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yao, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we provide the first report on several compns. of ternary Sn-Ge-Sb thin film alloys for application as sodium ion battery (aka NIB, NaB or SIB) anodes, employing Sn50Ge50, Sb50Ge50, and pure Sn, Ge, Sb as baselines. Sn50Ge25Sb25 also shows excellent rate capability, displaying a stable capacity of 381 mAhg-1 at a c.d. of 8500 mAg-1 (∼10C).  A survey of published literature indicates that 833 mAhg-1 is among the highest reversible capacities reported for a Sn-based NIB anode, while 381 mAhg-1 represents the optimum fast charge value. Comparing the microstructures of alloys where the capacity significantly exceeds the rule of mixts. prediction to those where it does not leads us to hypothesize that this new phenomenon originates from the Ge(Sn) that is able to sodiate beyond the 1:1 Na:Ge ratio reported for the pure element.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. alloying of sodium with silicon, lead and bismuth was studied by in-situ X-ray diffraction.  No evidence was found for sodium insertion into silicon at temps. up to 60°C.  Lead was found to catalytically decomp. electrolyte, hindering sodiation.  This could be avoided by applying a high current pulse to the cell to sodiate the lead surface.  Once the surface was sodiated, further sodiation of lead could proceed at low currents.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure Sn and a homogeneous nanocomposite of Sn and graphite (C), denoted as Sn/C, have been studied as a suitable anode for Na ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a facile chem. synthesis of monodisperse colloidal SnSb nanocrystals (NCs) via reaction between Sn NCs and SbCl3 in oleylamine under reducing conditions.  In comparison with individual Sn and Sb NCs and their mixts., we show that through the creation of SnSb alloyed NCs the Li-ion storage properties are enhanced due to combination of high cycling stability of Sb with higher specific Li-ion storage capacity of Sn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1. Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes. S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitra, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exfoliated MoS<sub>2</sub> Sheets and Reduced Graphene Oxide-An Excellent and Fast Anode for Sodium-ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Three dimensional (3D) MoS2 nanoflowers are successfully synthesized by hydrothermal method.  Further, a composite of as prepd. MoS2 nanoflowers and rGO is constructed by simple ultrasonic exfoliation technique.  The crystallog. and morphol. studies have been carried out by XRD, FE-SEM, TEM, HR-TEM and EDS etc.  Here, XRD study revealed, a composite of exfoliated MoS2 with expanded spacing of (002) crystal plane and rGO can be prepd. by simple 40 min of ultrasonic treatment. When tested as sodium-ion batteries anode material by applying two different potential windows, the composite demonstrates a high reversible specific capacity of 575 mAhg-1 at 100 mAg-1 in between 0.01 V-2.6 V and 218 mAhg-1 at 50 mAg-1 when discharged in a potential range of 0.4 V-2.6 V. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7147</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7155</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.6b00641</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Building Self-Healing Alloy Architecture for Stable Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes: A Case Study of Tin Anode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mao, Jianfeng; Fan, Xiulin; Luo, Chao; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7147-7155</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The rational design of anode materials is a challenge in developing sodium ion batteries.  Alloy anodes provide high gravimetric and volumetric capacities but suffer the short cycle life as a result of the continuous and accumulated pulverization, resulting from a large vol. change during the cycling process.  Herein, using pure Sn, an irreversible conversion reaction combined with an alloy reaction (SnO), and a reversible conversion reaction combined with an alloy reaction (Sn4P3) as samples, the pulverization and aggregation of the alloy anode can be partially recovered and the accumulation of pulverization and aggregation during charge/discharge cycles can be terminated using a reversible conversion reaction combined with an alloy reaction.  The cycling stability of three Sn-based anodes increases in order of Sn4P3 &gt; SnO &gt; Sn.  The enhancement in Sn4P3 can be attributed to a reversible reaction of Sn4P3 + 9Na ↔ 4Sn + 3Na3P, which repairs the cracks, damage, and aggregation of Sn particles that occurred in the alloy process of 4Sn + 15Na ↔ Na15Sn4 during cycling and, hence, terminates the pulverization.  The repair mechanism looks like the self-healing feature, where the damage can be healed by itself.  Therefore, the suggested mechanism can be called self-healing, while the repaired anode can be termed as the self-healing anode.  The use of self-healing strategies to build an electrode architecture is new and highly desirable because it can increase the cycle life and provide a general approach toward stable electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpWw5beIJBM1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liD7o5lQIBfmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjs1WjsL0%253D&amp;md5=b0bdee575b24a49017d3e87579d7c7a7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2013.05.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Baggetto, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Keum, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with long-term cycling attract increasing attention for large-scale energy storage.  However, traditional SIBs toward practical applications still suffer from low rate capability and poor cycle induced by pulverization and amorphorization of anodes at high rate (over 5 C) during the fast ion insertion/extn. process.  The present work demonstrates a robust strategy for a variety of (Sb-C, Bi-C, Sn-C, Ge-C, Sb-Bi-C) freestanding metal-carbon framework thin films via a space-confined superassembly (SCSA) strategy.  The sodium-ion battery employing the Sb-C framework exhibits an unprecedented performance with a high specific capacity of 246 mAh/g, long life cycle (5000 cycles), and superb capacity retention (almost 100%) at a high rate of 7.5 C (3.51A/g).  Further investigation indicates that the unique framework structure enables unusual reversible cryst.-phase transformation, guaranteeing the fast and long-cyclability sodium storage.                         rightTab-cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A highly stable (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene composite anode of sodium-ion batteries synthesized by oxygen plasma assisted milling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Deliang; Liu, Jiangwen; Li, Xiang; Hu, Renzong; Zeng, Meiqing; Yang, Lichun; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The (SnOx-Sn)@few layered graphene ((SnOx-Sn)@FLG) composite has been synthesized by O plasma-assisted milling.  Owing to the synergistic effect of rapid plasma heating and ball mill grinding, SnOx (1≤ x ≤2) nanoparticles generated from the reaction of Sn with O are tightly wrapped by FLG nanosheets which are simultaneously exfoliated from expanded graphite, forming secondary micro granules.  Inside the granules, the small size of the SnOx nanoparticles enables the fast kinetics for Na+ transfer.  The in-situ formed FLG and residual Sn nanoparticles improve the elec. cond. of the composite, meanwhile alleviate the aggregation of SnOx nanoparticles and relieve the vol. change during the cycling, which is beneficial for the cyclic stability for the Na+ storage.  As an anode material for Na-ion batteries, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 448 mAh/g at a c.d. of 100 mA/g in the 1st cycle, with 82.6% capacity retention after 250 cycles.  Even when the c.d. increases to 1000 mA/g, this composite retains 316.5 mAh/g after 250 cycles.  With superior Na+ storage stability, the (SnOx-Sn)@FLG composite can be a promising anode material for high performance sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpu3VJ7Z_IUi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljumziFT8rrIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkslyjtrY%253D&amp;md5=411e9333c9fa824c27eb67deca3362e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b14233"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal–Organic Framework-Derived NiSb Alloy Embedded in Carbon Hollow Spheres as Superior Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In the current research project, we have prepd. a novel Sb@C nanosphere anode with biomimetic yolk-shell structure for Li/Na-ion batteries via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement route.  The yolk-shell microstructure consists of Sb hollow yolk completely protected by a well-conductive carbon thin shell.  The substantial void space in the these hollow Sb@C yolk-shell particles allows for the full vol. expansion of inner Sb while maintaining the framework of the Sb@C anode and developing a stable SEI film on the outside carbon shell.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony has received a great deal of attention as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, this application is significantly hampered by inherent large vol. change and sluggish kinetics.  To address these issues, an antimony-cyano-based ionic liq.-derived nitrogen-doped carbon (Sb-CNC) hybrid is proposed and synthesized by ball-milling and subsequent pyrolysis treatment.  As an anode material for SIBs, the as-synthesized Sb-CNC hybrid delivers reversible capacities of 475 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and 203 mAh g-1 at 5000 mA g-1, and a 92.4% capacity retention based on the first-cycle capacity after 150 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  Using ex situ XPS and elemental mapping techniques, we attribute the good structural integrity to the formation of Sb-N-C bonds between Sb and the cyano-based ionic liq.-derived N-doped carbon matrix.  Moreover, the presence of N-doped carbon network in the hybrid material serves as a robust protective cover and an elec. highway, buffering the substantial vol. expansion of Sb nanoparticles and ensuring the fast electron transport for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0rTJNqWEUn7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljumziFT8rrIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktVKmsLc%253D&amp;md5=bdba7a23cb25ed9d8053b89fd94d27e2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA03434B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Si, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bao, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Uniformly-Distributed Sb Nanoparticles in Ionic Liquid-Derived Nitrogen-Enriched Carbon for Highly Reversible Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antinomy has received considerable attention as one of the most promising anode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity and suitable working voltage.  However, the large vol. change of Sb during the alloying/dealloying process causes poor cycling stability and low rate capability, which hinder its practical application.  Here, the authors substantially enhance the Na storage performance of Sb by binding Sb nanoparticles in ionic liq.-derived N-enriched C (Sb@NC) via pyrolysis of an SbCl3/1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium dicyanamide mixt.  The Sb@NC composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 440 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, superior rate performance of 285 and 237 mA h g-1 at the high current densities of 2 and 5 A g-1, resp., and greatly improved cycle life of 328 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 100 A g-1 after 300 cycles in the half cell of SIBs.  In the full cell, the energy d. of Sb@NC//Na3V2(PO4)3/C is ∼147 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 50 W kg-1.  Even at 2.37 kW kg-1, an energy d. of ∼65 W h kg-1 is still retained.  The remarkably improved electrochem. performance could be assigned to the synergistic effect of nanoscale size, uniform distribution, and chem. coupling effect between Sb and ionic liq.-derived N-enriched C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqodGGRdGl-4rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljumziFT8rrIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXosVCltrg%253D&amp;md5=58676af0e3ee4eb633c74aea69719a47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms3922"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, D.
